# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# gRPC Error Status Propagation Across Go Services

## Your Task

Compare how gRPC error status codes are created and propagated in kubernetes/kubernetes vs grafana/grafana vs etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that create gRPC Status errors with codes (codes.NotFound, codes.Internal, etc.) and the files that translate gRPC errors to HTTP responses.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

56-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of how gRPC error status codes are created and propagated across the three repositories. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings on gRPC error status propagation across:

### **kubernetes/kubernetes**
- **Error Creation**: Uses inline `status.Error()` and `status.Errorf()` with codes like `codes.ResourceExhausted`, `codes.NotFound`, `codes.InvalidArgument`
- **HTTP Translation**: Two-tier approach:
  1. **CRI Streaming** (`staging/src/k8s.io/kubelet/pkg/cri/streaming/errors.go`): `WriteError()` function maps gRPC codes to HTTP
  2. **gRPC-Gateway** (`vendor/github.com/grpc-ecosystem/grpc-gateway/v2/runtime/errors.go`): `HTTPStatusFromCode()` provides comprehensive mapping

### **grafana/grafana**
- **Error Creation**: Focus on authentication/authorization with `codes.Unauthenticated`, `codes.NotFound` in interceptors and service layers
- **Status Translation** (`pkg/tsdb/influxdb/fsql/fsql.go`): Converts gRPC codes to internal backend status codes via switch statement matching

### **etcd-io/etcd**
- **Error Definition**: Centralized approach in `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go` with pre-defined errors for each code type
- **Error Translation** (`server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go`): `togRPCError()` function uses explicit mapping table (`toGRPCErrorMap`) from internal domain errors to gRPC status errors
- **Consistent Codes**: All codes clearly documented (InvalidArgument, FailedPrecondition, NotFound, OutOfRange, ResourceExhausted, Unavailable, DataLoss, PermissionDenied, Unauthenticated, Canceled, DeadlineExceeded)

The analysis includes 28 files and 10 key symbols that demonstrate the error propagation chains in each system.

(ErrGRPCWatchCanceled, ErrGRPCCanceled)\\n- `codes.DeadlineExceeded` for timeouts (ErrGRPCDeadlineExceeded)\\n\\n**Error Translation Pattern:**\\netcd translates internal errors to gRPC errors using a mapping system (server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go):\\n- `togRPCError()` function converts internal domain errors to pre-defined gRPC status errors\\n- Maintains mapping in `toGRPCErrorMap` from internal errors (membership, mvcc, auth, etc.) to gRPC errors\\n- Falls back to `status.Error(codes.Unknown, ...)` for unmapped errors\\n- Special handling for context errors (context.Canceled \u2192 codes.Canceled, context.DeadlineExceeded \u2192 codes.DeadlineExceeded)\\n\\n**Error Checking Pattern:**\\netcd client and proxy layers check status codes using `status.FromError()` to determine retry behavior and error handling:\\n- `client/v3/retry.go`: Checks if error is retryable based on code (e.g., unavailable, internal)\\n- `client/v3/watch.go`: Checks for FailedPrecondition to handle cancellation\\n- `client/v3/client.go`: Determines retry eligibility by checking code != Unavailable && code != Internal\\n- `server/proxy/grpcproxy/watch.go` and `lease.go`: Check for Canceled code to detect connection closure\\n\\n### Cross-Repository Patterns\\n\\n**Common Pattern:**\\n1. **Error Creation**: All three repos use `google.golang.org/grpc/status.Error()` or `.Errorf()` with specific codes\\n2. **Error Propagation**: Errors flow from business logic \u2192 gRPC handlers \u2192 transport layer\\n3. **Status Extraction**: `status.FromError()` extracts status info for inspection\\n4. **Code-Based Handling**: Switch statements on `status.Code()` determine behavior\\n5. **Translation**: Each repo handles translation differently:\\n   - Kubernetes: Uses both simple switch (CRI) and comprehensive mapping (gRPC-Gateway)\\n   - Grafana: Maps to internal backend status codes\\n   - etcd: Pre-allocates all errors with codes, maps internal errors \u2192 gRPC errors\\n\\n**Key Difference:**\\netcd's approach of pre-defining all errors in a centralized registry (rpctypes/error.go) and maintaining explicit mappings differs from Kubernetes' and Grafana's inline error creation patterns. This makes etcd's error handling more consistent and easier to audit.\"\n}\n",
